<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">yard</strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">yards</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A small, usually uncultivated area adjoining or (now especially) within the precincts of a house or other building.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1913</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_C._Lincoln" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Joseph C. Lincoln">Joseph C. Lincoln</a>,  chapter 1, in  <cite><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://openlibrary.org/works/OL5535161W">Mr. Pratt's Patients</a></cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">'Twas early June, the new grass was flourishing everywheres, the posies in the <b>yard</b>â€”peonies and suchâ€”in full bloom, the sun was shining, and the water of the bay was blue, with light green streaks where the shoal showed.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">US</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada" class="extiw" title="w:Canada">Canada</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia" class="extiw" title="w:Australia">Australia</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The property surrounding one's house, typically dominated by one's lawn.
<dl><dd><span class="nyms synonym"><span class="defdate">Synonym:</span> <span class="Latn" lang="en">garden</span> <span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content qualifier-content">UK</span><span class="ib-brac qualifier-brac">)</span></span></dd></dl></li>
<li>An enclosed area designated for a specific purpose, e.g. on farms, railways etc.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1931</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Palmer_(author)" class="extiw" title="w:John Palmer (author)">Francis Beeding</a>,  â€œ2/2â€, in  <cite>Death Walks in Eastrepps</cite> | <sup><a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://openlibrary.org/works/OL6342782W">[1]</a></sup>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">A little further on, to the right, was a large garage, where the charabancs stood, half in and half out of the <b>yard</b>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>A place where moose or deer herd together in winter for pasture, protection, etc.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jamaican_English" class="extiw" title="w:Jamaican English">Jamaican</a></span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Oneâ€™s house or home.</li></ol>

<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verb">Verb</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">yard</strong> (<i>third-person singular simple present</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en 3 | s | pres-form-of" lang="en">yards</b>, <i>present participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en pres | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">yarding</b>, <i>simple past and past participle</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en past | and | past | ptcp-form-of" lang="en">yarded</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">transitive</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> To confine to a yard.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1893</b>,  Elijah Kellogg,  <cite>Good old times, or, Grandfather's struggles for a homestead</cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">As they reached the door, Bose, having <b>yarded</b> the cows, was stealing around the corner of the pig-sty, and making for the woods.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li></ol>
<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_2">Etymology 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>From <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English" class="extiw" title="w:Middle English">Middle English</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">Èerde</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">yerd</i>, <i class="Latn mention" lang="enm">Èerd</i>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_English" class="extiw" title="w:Old English">Old English</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="ang">Ä¡ierd</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">â€œ</span><span class="mention-gloss">branch; rod, staff; measuring stick; yardland</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">â€</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, from <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" class="extiw" title="w:Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a></span> <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*gazdijÅ</i>, from <i class="Latinx mention" lang="gem-pro">*gazdaz</i>. Cognate with <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dutch_language" class="extiw" title="w:Dutch language">Dutch</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="nl">gard</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">â€œ</span><span class="mention-gloss">twig</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">â€</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>, <span class="etyl"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language" class="extiw" title="w:German language">German</a></span> <i class="Latn mention" lang="de">Gerte</i> and probably related to Latin <i class="Latn mention" lang="la">hasta</i> <span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">(</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">â€œ</span><span class="mention-gloss">spear</span><span class="mention-gloss-double-quote">â€</span><span class="mention-gloss-paren annotation-paren">)</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="cite_note-1"> | 1 | </a></sup>
</p>

<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_2">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">yard</strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">yards</b>)
</p>
<ol><li>A unit of length equal to 3 feet in the US customary and British imperial systems of measurement, equal to precisely 0.9144 m since 1959 (US) or 1963 (UK).
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1913</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_C._Lincoln" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Joseph C. Lincoln">Joseph C. Lincoln</a>,  chapter 1, in  <cite><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://openlibrary.org/works/OL5535161W">Mr. Pratt's Patients</a></cite>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">Thinks I to myself,  | Sol, you're run off your course again. This is a rich man's summer  | cottage | <span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>â€¦<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>. |  So I started to back away again into the bushes. But I hadn't backed more'n a couple of <b>yards</b> when I see something so amazing that I couldn't help scooching down behind the bayberries and looking at it.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li>Units of similar composition or length in other systems.</li>
<li class="senseid" id="English-nautical"><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">nautical</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> Any spar carried aloft.
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">nautical</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A long tapered timber hung on a mast to which is bent a sail, and may be further qualified as a square, lateen, or lug yard. The first is hung at right angles to the mast, the latter two hang obliquely.</li></ol></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A branch, twig, or shoot.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A staff, rod, or stick.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete<span class="ib-comma">,</span> medicine</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> A penis.
<ul><li><div class="citation-whole"><span class="cited-source"><b>1603</b>,  <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michel_de_Montaigne" class="extiw" title="w:Michel de Montaigne">Michel de Montaigne</a>,  chapter 12, in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Florio" class="extiw" title="w:John Florio">John Florio</a>, transl., <cite><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Essays_(Montaigne)" class="extiw" title="w:Essays (Montaigne)">The Essayes,<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">[</span></span><span title="or, Morall, Politike and Millitarie Discourses of Lo. Michaell de Montaigne, Knight of the Noble Order of St. Michaell, and One of the Gentlemen in Ordinary of the French King, Henry the Third His Chamber">â€¦</span><span class="q-hellip-b"><span style="font-style: normal;">]</span></span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span></a></cite>, book II, printed at London |  By <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Valentine_Simmes" class="extiw" title="w:Valentine Simmes">Val[entine] Simmes</a> for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Blount" class="extiw" title="w:Edward Blount">Edward Blount</a><span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span><span title="dwelling in Paules churchyard">â€¦</span><span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>, <small><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC" class="extiw" title="w:OCLC">OCLC</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://worldcat.org/oclc/946730821">946730821</a></small>:</span><dl><dd><div class="h-quotation"><span class="Latn e-quotation" lang="en">there were some people found who tooke pleasure to unhood the end of their <b>yard</b>, and to cut off the fore-skinne after the manner of the Mahometans and Jewes<span class="q-hellip-sp"> </span><span class="q-hellip-b">[</span>â€¦<span class="q-hellip-b">]</span><span class="q-hellip-b"></span>.</span></div></dd></dl></div></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">US</a><span class="ib-comma">,</span> slang<span class="ib-comma">,</span> uncommon</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> 100 dollars.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The yardland, an obsolete English unit of land roughly understood as 30 acres.
<ul><li><i>a.</i> <b>1634</b>, W. Noye, <i>The Complete Lawyer</i>, 57:
<dl><dd>You must note, that two Fardells of Land make a Nooke of Land, and two Nookes make halfe a <b>Yard</b> of Land.</dd></dl></li></ul></li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The rod, a surveying unit of (once) 15 or (now) 16<s style="display:none">+</s><small><sup>1</sup><big>â„</big><sub>2</sub></small> feet.</li>
<li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">obsolete</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> The rood, area bound by a square rod, <small><sup>1</sup><big>â„</big><sub>4</sub></small> acre.</li></ol>

<hr><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_3">Etymology 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h3>
<p>Clipping of <i class="Latn mention" lang="en">milliard</i>.
</p>
<hr><h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_3">Noun</span><span class="mw-editsection"></span></h4>
<p><strong class="Latn headword" lang="en">yard</strong> (<i>plural</i> <b class="Latn form-of lang-en p-form-of" lang="en">yards</b>)
</p>
<ol><li><span class="ib-brac">(</span><span class="ib-content">finance</span><span class="ib-brac">)</span> 10<sup>9</sup>, A <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_and_short_scales" class="extiw" title="w:Long and short scales">short scale</a> billion; a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Long_and_short_scales" class="extiw" title="w:Long and short scales">long scale</a> thousand millions or milliard.
<dl><dd><i>I need to hedge a <b>yard</b> of yen.</i></dd></dl></li></ol>
